The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Reduce the Heavy Cigarette Tax in Sichuan Province 135

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, stating: "To the Ministry of Finance: On the 31st of this month, we received a letter from the Cigarette Factory Industry Association of Zhabei. According to a letter from the Jingcun Cigarette Company in Wanxian, Sichuan, various cigarette taxes and levies are harsh, making development difficult. Repeated requests to the Sichuan Provincial Government for appropriate reductions have been ineffective. Therefore, a special representative has been sent to Shanghai to request assistance, and a special report has been submitted to your association, requesting assistance. Please investigate and grant assistance to alleviate the difficulties of businesses." The association inquired, "Your Ministry previously issued a consultation to the Hubei Provincial Government regarding the case of heavy cigarette tax in Xiangyang, Hubei, stating that according to the General Cigarette Tax Regulations, all cigarettes that have paid the unified tax and have sufficient stamps affixed are allowed to be sold in various provinces and concessions, and no additional taxes or levies may be imposed. If additional fees or levies are imposed on cigarettes that have already paid the unified tax, whether collected from consumers or from cigarette factories and managers, it is considered double taxation, and merchants may present evidence of the double taxation to request a tax refund. In essence, it is no different from seizing national treasury revenue to enrich local coffers. Please issue a strict order to stop the tax." The miscellaneous taxes in Sichuan Province are even harsher than those in Hubei. Based on the previous letter, it is appropriate to cable your Ministry to investigate and verify the matter and to consult the Sichuan Provincial Supervisor Liu to stop the double taxation for the sake of public convenience. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows."

Eleven Umbrella Factories, Including Huali, Suddenly Shut Down 136

Workers Are Panic-Stricken

Petitioning the Party Department for Assistance

Eleven umbrella factories, including Huali at No. 366, Republic Road, and other factories such as Fengli, Minhua Sen, etc., recently suddenly shut down at the same time. More than 400 workers from various factories were panicking and sent representatives to the Municipal Party Department yesterday to petition. The details are as follows:

Sudden Shutdown Eleven umbrella factories in this city, including Huali, Fengli, Minhua Sen, Dongnan, Nanchang, Sanyuan, Zhixin Ruilin, New World, Dayouyu, and Tailai, suddenly announced their shutdown at the same time on the previous day (the 31st). The workers had no prior knowledge of this, and the factories did not announce the reasons for the shutdown. For a time, the workers in various factories were panicking and reported to the Umbrella Industry Association, requesting assistance. According to an investigation by a reporter from the Dagon News Agency, it is said that someone recently planned to establish a public sales market for the umbrella industry, which is quite detrimental to the business of various factories. Therefore, the factories unanimously shut down to express their firm opposition.

Workers' Petition At 2:00 PM yesterday, representatives from various factories, including Zhu Jiming, Liu Changsheng, Lu Zhenqi, Shen Xiangfa, Qi Xiaolin, Cai Linzhi, Gao Shude, Zhu Guosheng, Lu Amao, Ding Bolang, and Xu Ziyu, totaling eleven people, went to the Municipal Party Department to petition. Li Weixiong, a cadre of the People's Movement Section, received them. The workers recounted that the sudden closure of the factories would affect the livelihood of more than 400 workers and requested that the Party Department quickly investigate the truth and order the factories to resume operations immediately. Mr. Li said that he would accept the request and promised to send personnel to investigate together with the Social Affairs Bureau on Monday and take action immediately. The representatives originally planned to petition the Social Affairs Bureau as well, but because yesterday was Saturday and the Bureau was not open for business in the afternoon, they changed the date to tomorrow.

U.S. Destroyer Collides with French Gunboat 137

The French shallow-water gunboat "Francis Garnier," which was anchored in the Huangpu River, was ordered to move elsewhere yesterday. It raised anchor at 2:00 PM in the afternoon to exit. When it reached the river outside the Ruirong Iron Factory in Pudong, it happened to encounter the U.S. Destroyer No. 227 entering Shanghai. Both ships were anchored and turning around in the same place and could not avoid each other, resulting in the bow of the U.S. ship violently colliding with the middle of the starboard side of the French ship. With a loud bang, a large hole, about five or six feet high and seven or eight feet wide, was punched in the French ship. The deckhouse and the second deck were completely destroyed. The stairway next to the deckhouse and a small boat and a ventilator on the second deck were all smashed. Fortunately, the bow of the U.S. ship was convex above and concave below, so the damage to the French ship was five or six feet above the waterline. If it had hit the lower part, the river water would have flooded in and the ship would have sunk. After the accident, the French ship temporarily stopped its exit and returned to the bank of the Pudong Lujiazui East First Taitong Coal Depot for temporary mooring, waiting to be repaired in the dock.

The Mourning of the Death of Guan's Mother 138

The mother of Guan Gongzhi, the District Chief of the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Madam He, was brought to Shanghai from Guangdong by District Chief Guan when he took office in this city in order to fulfill his filial piety. Unexpectedly, his mother was old and her old illness recurred from time to time. District Chief Guan personally hired doctors to attend to her and administer medicine. For several months, he worked tirelessly day and night. However, the doctors were helpless, and the medicine was ineffective. She passed away on March 31st at Maoshi (5-7 AM). The great coffin was personally viewed and placed in the coffin at the Chinese Funeral Parlor in Haig Road at Wushi (11 AM - 1 PM) on April 1st. After encoffining, it was temporarily placed in the parlor, and a date was chosen to hold a wake and transport the coffin back to his hometown for burial next to the ancestral tomb. Hundreds of people, including chiefs of various departments of the municipal government, colleagues, and relatives and friends in Shanghai, attended the memorial service.

Zhou Xiangling and Others Relieve Farmers in Their Hometowns 139

Initiating the Organization of a Farmer Relief Association

Nanxun Town in Wuxing County, Zhejiang Province, and Zhenze Town in Wujiang County, Jiangsu Province, are both well-known production areas of Zhili natural silk in our country. Farmers in both places rely on this for a large portion of their annual income. In the past, during the golden age, farmers were quite well-off, and local commerce also relied on it to prosper. Therefore, the gentry and people of both towns were known for their wealth. In recent years, due to the attraction of rayon and the international sales being plundered by countries such as Japan, the price of silk has plummeted, almost to the point where no one cares. The rural economy has therefore gone bankrupt. Moreover, due to the influence of the current situation, disasters have struck frequently. Yuan Hong (fields) are everywhere, and the hungry cannot get clothing and food, and the sick cannot get medical treatment. The misery of the situation is unprecedented. Now, prominent figures from both places in Shanghai, including Zhou Xiangling, Chu Minyi, Lu Liankui, Xu Pucheng, Xu Zhaonian, and Tan Songtao, concerned about their hometowns, have made a great wish, with hearts that feel the hunger and drowning of others as if it were their own. They have initiated the organization of a Farmer Relief Association. In addition to their own donations, they are also widely soliciting donations from enthusiastic people in both places, hoping to raise a large amount of money to quickly seek relief. This work is already in full swing. It is heard that there are many people from both places living abroad who are renowned in political and business circles, and there are even more who possess large sums of money. Since this concerns the relief of their hometowns, they will definitely enthusiastically contribute and jointly participate in this righteous cause. This is truly good news for the farmers of both places.

Three Children's Corpses Found in the Huangpu River 142

At around 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, three children's corpses were found in the Suzhou River between the Fujian Road Bridge and the Zhejiang Road Bridge. The largest was about one year old, the next seemed to be less than one year old, and the smallest was born not long ago. The three corpses drifted with the tide, not far from each other. They were discovered by Customs water police officers No. 91 and No. 119, who separately retrieved the corpses and sent them to the Nanshi Life Saving Bureau for collection. It was found that the three children's corpses were likely suffering from the same epidemic plague and died, and their families threw them into the river.

Page 14

A Fire in More Than 100 Straw Shed Boats on Moganshan Road 143

Spreading to Nine Workshops of the Xinda Flour Mill

An Elderly Man and a Girl Missing

At the end of Moganshan Road in Shanghai West, on the south bank of Suzhou Road (opposite the Tongyi Yarn Factory), there were about 180 small boats docked, with straw sheds built on the shore, connected to each other for protection from wind and rain and for access. Most of the residents were small vendors from Jiangbei, rickshaw pullers, and workers from nearby factories. At around 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon, a boat dweller surnamed Liu accidentally started a fire while cooking lunch. Because most of these boats were covered with reed mats and straw sheds, sparks flew in all directions. At this time, the northeast wind was very strong, so the fire quickly became uncontrollable. In no time, all the boats were completely burned. When the fire was at its fiercest, a reed mat shed caught fire and was blown by the wind to the roof of the Xinda Flour Mill's workshop to the south, which immediately caught fire as well. A total of nine workshops were also completely burned, and the fire spread to two piles of wheat stored at the adjacent Fufeng Flour Mill. When the fire broke out, the Central Fire Brigade was notified and immediately dispatched the Jing'an Temple Fire Station to drive to the scene to put out the fire. It was not until around 4:00 PM that the fire was extinguished. After investigation, the Xinda Flour Mill suffered losses worth about 5,000 to 6,000 yuan, and the Fufeng Mill suffered less damage. However, only the bottoms of all the boats remained. Fortunately, the fire broke out during the day, so all the residents and the workers of the Xinda workshop were able to escape. Although a few people were injured while running, the injuries were minor. It was also heard that in one boat dweller's family, an elderly man and a young girl did not escape. However, after the fire was extinguished, no corpses were found. Whether they were burned to death in the fire or fell into the river and drowned remains to be investigated.

The Robbery and Murder of a Patrol Officer Case Begins Trial 144

The Second Special Court Attaches Great Importance to This Case

Sending Personnel to Survey the Scene and Draw a Map

The robbers Yu Tingrong and Zheng Ziming, both from Ningbo, together with Tang Xinhua, who is still at large, used weapons on the evening of January 30th of this year at 1:15 AM to rob Zhu Chunlin, a pedestrian, of a Walter Tweed jacket and two yuan in cash in his pocket in a dark and secluded place outside the back door of the Killing Cow Company on Croc Road in the French Concession. They carried the stolen goods and fled north. When they reached the intersection of Mintini Road and Fada Avenue in front of the Golden Great Theater, the victim followed behind and reported to the patrol officer Wang Jigui, No. 614, who was on duty. The patrol officer stepped forward and ordered the robbers Yu to stop and raise their hands for inspection. Unexpectedly, the two robbers Zheng and Tang in front, a few feet away, Zheng immediately fired a shot to resist arrest. The bullet hit patrol officer Wang in the head, and he fell to the ground. He died before he could be treated. The special agency supervisors Jin Jiulin, Chief Detective Zhang Ziying, and the patrol detectives then investigated the pedestrians.

Robbery and Murder of a Patrolman Case Opens 145

The Second Special Court Attaches Great Importance to This Case

Sending Personnel to the Scene to Survey and Draw Diagrams

The robbers Yu Tingrong and Zheng Ziming, both from Ningbo, along with Tang Xinhua (still at large), on the night of January 30th, at 1:15 AM, wielding weapons, robbed the pedestrian Zhu Chunlin of a Tweed overcoat and two dollars and two cents in foreign currency outside the back door of the Slaughterhouse Company on Rue de la Grosse in the French Concession, a dark and secluded spot. They fled north with the loot. As the victim followed them to the intersection of Avenue de l'Amiral Thierry and Avenue Edward VII, in front of the Golden Theatre, he reported to Patrolman No. 614, Wang Weigui, who was on duty. The patrolman stepped forward and ordered the robbers to stop and raise their hands for inspection. However, Zheng and Tang, who were several feet ahead, Zheng immediately fired a shot to resist arrest. The bullet struck Patrolman Wang in the head, and he fell to the ground, dying before medical help could arrive. Immediately, special agents Jin Jiulin and Zhang Ziying, along with patrolmen on duty, examined the arriving pedestrians and, upon hearing the news, rushed to the scene. They first apprehended Yu, then arrested Zheng at the staircase of the Siming Hotel on Avenue Edward VII near Rue de la Soie. They also confiscated a pistol and dozens of bullets from his room, taking them to the police station. The next day, the police station reported to Prosecutor Deng of the Second Special Court, who examined Wang's body at the morgue. The body was released to his family for burial. Meanwhile, the police station, having discovered that Yu and his accomplices had committed crimes at the Slaughterhouse Company three times, summoned all the victims and escorted Yu and Zheng to the Second Special District Court. They were prosecuted for robbery and murder under Articles 348 and 285, Section 1 of the Criminal Law. The court appointed lawyers Lu Shaozong and Shan Yuhua to defend the two defendants. The various court sessions that have taken place without a conclusion have been reported previously. Now, it is learned that the presiding judge of the criminal court, Wang Gangxu, considering the seriousness of the case, invited lawyer Shan Yuhua, who defends the two robbers, and notified the police department to send Detective Zhang Ziying and patrolmen to escort Yu and Zheng. Judge Wang himself accompanied the court clerk to the scene of the incident in front of the Golden Theatre to conduct an on-site inspection, ordering the two robbers to reenact the scene of being stopped by the patrolman and the shooting. They also drew a map of the locations where the victim, the patrolman, and the two robbers were standing. They also inspected the robbery scene for a week. After returning to the court, the original plan was to continue the trial the day before yesterday, but due to the large number of cases, there was not enough time. It was changed to 10:15 AM yesterday, when Judge Wang, along with Prosecutor Deng Bao and Clerk Ren Qiyuan, specially opened the Fourth Tribunal for the trial. The lawyers Lu and Shan, who were appointed to defend the defendants, also arrived in court on time. Lawyer Fei Xizhen appeared in court on behalf of the police department. After the judge took the bench, he first ordered the bailiffs to bring Yu and Zheng to the defendant's position. Then, he summoned the victim Zhu Chunlin and Wang Jinsheng (the first victim of the robbery, Hua Xingsheng, originally lived on Guangxi Road and has moved away, making it impossible to summon him) to court, asking about the circumstances of the robbery. He also asked Zhu Chunlin about following the robbers to the Golden Theatre and reporting them to the police, and the robbers opening fire. He also summoned the father of the deceased patrolman, Wang Gusheng, and his wife for questioning. Then, he questioned the defendant Yu Tingrong, who confessed that on that night, Zheng Ziming held the gun, and Tang Xinhua, who is still at large, stripped the victim of his clothes. He, Yu, was keeping watch. After the robbery, Tang and Zheng were in front, and he was behind. When they reached the entrance of the Golden Theatre, a patrolman shouted at him to raise his hands for inspection. He immediately raised his hands and allowed the inspection. Suddenly, he heard a gunshot, and the patrolman fell to the ground. He also said that he had been keeping watch during the previous two robberies. When Zheng Ziming was questioned, he confessed that the gun was given to him by Tang Xinhua, who is still at large. After the robbery, he and Tang were in front, and Yu was behind. When they reached the entrance of the Golden Theatre, he heard the patrolman shouting at Yu to raise his hands for inspection, and he also heard the pedestrian shouting to catch the robbers. Tang told him to shoot, but he refused. At this time, he was holding the gun in his right hand, tucked under his left armpit. Tang came to snatch the gun, and the bullet flew out, hitting the patrolman. After repeated rebuttals in court for an hour and a half, the court ordered the start of the debate. Lawyer Fei from the police department and the two defense lawyers Lu and Shan debated for a long time. The court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the eighth day. By the time the clerk finished reading the confession and adjourned the court, the clock had struck two.

Police Find Communist Propaganda Cloth 148

Containing More Than 161,000 Characters

But Chen Shuying Insists It Is Not Hers

According to the North China Daily News, the Special Branch of the Public Security Department of the Public Concession recently cracked a Communist Party organ within the Concession, discovering a large number of traces of documents. However, after applying chemicals, the handwriting was revealed, which seemed to belong to the general agency of the Chinese Communist Party, that is, all the documents of the National Federation of Trade Unions. The organ was located upstairs in a cigarette paper shop at No. 290, Rue Amiral Bayle. The occupants were Chen Guang and his wife, and Chen's sister Shuying. Chen Guang and his wife had escaped, so only Chen Shuying was arrested. At the time of the arrest, the detectives found a lot of white-bottomed willow cloth and white paper in her room. Afterwards, a handkerchief found in the room was handed over to the Special Branch for chemical treatment, and the principles of Communist propaganda in the Kuomintang army written in Chinese were discovered. Then, several pieces of white-bottomed willow cloth were taken and subjected to the same chemical experiment, and there was no one without handwriting. The contents were all Communist Party leaflets, notices, and books. The method of shooting machine guns and throwing bombs in the sky calculated that there were forty-three pieces of cloth, about twenty-seven inches wide, and forty-three feet long in total. It is estimated that each foot has three thousand seven hundred and fifty characters, then forty-three feet have a total of one hundred and sixty-one thousand two hundred and fifty characters. At the end of each paragraph, the type of content is written, except for several leaflets about the Shanghai Commemoration Day and the January 28th Songhu Battle, the rest are all records of the Communist Party's activities in Manchuria, Hunan, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hebei, Fujian, Qin, and Henan provinces. In addition, thirty-eight copies of Red Flag Weekly were seized, the earliest of which was published in December 1931, and the most recent of which was published on March 8 of this year. It is heard that the cloth contains the actual records of the National Federation of Trade Unions' work in the past two years. A lot of white paper and light yellow paper, as well as many blank practice books, were also found in the room, all of which are thought to have handwriting. Chen Shuying, who was arrested, speaks Russian and insisted that the items found by the detectives were stored by her father's friend, surnamed Yu.

Li Changqing Swindles Money 152

丨Sentenced to Three Months Imprisonment丨

Bao Kang, the six-year-old son of Shen Shenti, a Ningbo native residing at No. 58, Rixin Lane, Tangshan Road, was playing in the alley at 3:30 PM on February 18 when he was lured away and disappeared. Shen only had this son and loved him dearly, so he posted a reward notice at the entrance, saying, "If anyone can send the child back, they will be handsomely rewarded." Later, Li Changqing, a Zhenjiang native, took this opportunity to falsely claim to Shen that his son Bao Kang had been found at the home of a certain family outside the South Gate of Huzhou and came to inform him that he was willing to accompany him to find him there. Shen believed it to be true and went to Huzhou with him, staying in a hotel. All expenses were borne by Li. Later, according to Li Changqing, the child was at the Chen family's home and required 500 yuan before he would be handed over. Shen had no money. After repeated consultations, the result was reduced to 150 yuan. Shen said that he had to see the child first before he would prepare the money and take him back. But Li knew that everything he said was false, so he could not do it. He made an excuse to return together. On March 19, Li Changqing went to Shen's place again and asked him to hand over 150 yuan, saying that he would guarantee to send his son back. Shen anticipated that it was still false and suspected that Li had kidnapped him. He immediately handed Li over to Detective Shen Binkui and took him to the Huishan Police Station, which transferred him to the First Special District Court for interrogation. Because Li Changqing insisted that he was actually kidnapped by his friend Chen Jibiao, a native of Huzhou, Chen had been captured by the Public Security Bureau there. He was ordered to return to prison for a detailed investigation at a later date. Yesterday, Judge Xiao Xiefen came to court for a follow-up interrogation. Police lawyer Zhang Dayin said that during the postponement, police detectives accompanied the defendant to Huzhou to arrest Chen, but Li could not point out the location. Now the county government there has replied, saying that there is no such person as Chen. He will present the letter for inspection. However, according to the police investigation, the child Bao Kang was not kidnapped by Li. He is now prosecuted for fraud and theft under Article 370, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. When the defendant was questioned, his confession was evasive and he asked for leniency. Judge Xiao ruled that Li Changqing should be sentenced to three months of imprisonment. The number of days of custody before the verdict is determined shall be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day.

Qingpu Ship Engine Malfunction 153

Causing a One-Day Delay

The Qingpu ship of the Sanbei Company's Yangtze River route, which came to Shanghai from Hankou on the afternoon of the 30th of last month, docked at Wharf No. 2 in Nanshi, No. 16, to load and unload goods. Yesterday morning (1st) at about 3 o'clock, both passengers and goods were loaded, so it raised its anchor and set off for Hankou. Shortly after leaving the dock, because it was high tide and the current was very rapid, the hull was pushed back, causing the lead wire rope tied to the No. 2 River Jian Fudong Transportation Office to wrap around the engine leaves. The engine leaves immediately failed, and the ship could not move forward. Fortunately, it was discovered early. When the shipowner learned of this, he ordered the ship to stop. At dawn, he hired a waterman to go into the water and completely remove the lead wire entangled in the engine leaves. The ship then immediately sailed to the Hongsheng Wharf in Pudong to dock. He reported to the company. Upon receiving the news, the company sent personnel to the ship in the afternoon to inspect it. There was no damage. The passengers did not disembark and were changed to export to Hankou this morning.

Interrogation and Judgment of Luring Women into Prostitution 154

丨Zhang Lin and Wang Laosi are Sentenced Separately丨

Li Wanjin, a woman from Zhenjiang, is fifteen years old and has a slightly pretty appearance. She lost her parents when she was young, so she was raised by her aunt Wang Qin since she was six years old. In June of last year, two fellow villagers, Wang A'er and Wei Langen, lured her to Shanghai and sold her to Wang Laosi, a woman who opened a pheasant brothel at No. 609, North Hai Road, for more than 100 yuan as an adopted daughter. Every night, she was forced to solicit customers on Sixth Avenue to sell prostitution. If she did not get her wish, she would be beaten severely. Although the woman suffered grievances, she had no way to escape the fire pit. Recently, her cousin Xu Gongquan, who had opened a barber shop on Xinzha Road, learned that his cousin had been abducted and sold to Wang as a pheasant, so he tried his best to find out the truth and reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. The police station ordered Detective Wang Jiaju to go to the address to arrest her. Because it was about 3 AM this morning, Wang's lover, Zhang Linbao, was also arrested, and the woman was rescued and taken back. At about 9 o'clock, Wang Laosi and Zhang Linbao were escorted to the First Special District Local Court Criminal Court. The head of the Criminal Court, Feng Shide, took the seat and mentioned the situation at the time. Police lawyer Ru Baoyi got up and stated that Feng Shide then interrogated Zhang Linbao, who confessed that he was 38 years old and was related to Wang Laosi. There was no relationship between husband and wife. He lived in the French Concession and had a wife and children. Because there were relatives coming to his home that day, he could not accommodate himself, so he temporarily stayed at that place. He did not order the woman to sell prostitution. According to Wang Laosi's confession, the woman's father brought her last year and discussed with my father to let her sell prostitution in my place. Her father took the night's earnings. As for Zhang, he is my cousin. When the detectives came to arrest him, he was the only one lying on my bed. According to Li Wanjin's confession, my parents died a long time ago. In June of last year, I was abducted by fellow villagers Wang A'er and Wei Langen in my hometown and sold to Wang's place in Fula, Shanghai, to serve as a pheasant. Every night, I received guests and the night's earnings were two or three yuan, and the money was taken by Wang. Zhang Linmai is indeed her husband. According to Xu Gongquan's statement, Judge Feng then announced the verdict in court. Zhang Linbao jointly induced a woman under the age of sixteen to commit adultery, and was sentenced to six months of imprisonment. Wang Laosi jointly induced a woman under the age of sixteen to commit adultery, and was sentenced to six months of imprisonment. Wang Laosi jointly induced a woman under the age of sixteen to commit adultery and was sentenced to one year of imprisonment. The number of days of custody before the judgment is determined will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day. Li Wanjin will be temporarily handed over to Jiliang for adoption.

Reader Advisory

On the Power of Supply and Western Civilization, Part 3 164

From Mr. Xu Xianfu of this city:

The letter I wrote to you on the fourteenth has not yet fully expressed my desires. Today, I dare to present my humble opinions again for your consideration. I hope you will allow me to do so.

My repeated letters are all concerned with the well-being of the nation and the masses. Everything I have discussed is, in my opinion, superior to problems such as suicide, attachment to love, occupation, and inheritance. The latter are aimed at individual selfishness, not the urgent needs of the entire nation and all the people. Some may say that these problems are indeed related to individual selfishness, but they are also caused by the social environment. The so-called salvation is precisely the meaning of "accumulating private interests for the public good." Who knows that this is the inferior root of capitalist tradition, and the reason for the destruction of capitalism today? Now that we know that society is evil, we should judge its outward manifestations and seek fundamental reforms. The so-called eradication from the root will make trivial problems disappear. Why bother to follow the uneconomical and incomplete method of treating the head when it hurts and the foot when it hurts, and be ridiculed for being superficial? Moreover, the implementers of socialism must "turn their backs on selfishness for the public good." The liberation of Chinese farmers and workers, the revitalization of the Chinese nation, and the realization of international peace cannot allow any more selfishness to exist among them. However, there are many ways to reform, and people's opinions differ. Without a unified revolutionary theory, there will be no consistent revolutionary behavior. So, what should we take and what should we abandon? The youth of the popular vanguard and the public opinion that leads society have no room for shirking their responsibility. Public opinion advocates that the goal of the youth revolution lies in the laboring masses, but the tool of the revolution lies in the youth. It is not permissible to mistake the means for the end, nor is it appropriate to regard the end as the means. Therefore, valuing the youth issue is no less important than the issue of the laboring masses. This is the meaning of my sincere appeals to my peers.

Now that we know the importance of revolutionary theory, what is the way to take and abandon? First and foremost, research. We should use an observational eye to analyze a theory through experience, and then measure it against the facts. It should be carried out in both time and space, and should be valued. One must not immediately add contempt or blindly follow a general concept. I have often read your teachings, and between the lines, there is a sense of longing for socialism. Indeed, capitalism is bankrupt, and we will eventually have to find a way out. Socialism is certainly good, but should we not regard it as the progress of capitalism? Let's trace the history of socialism. Its ideas have been around since the rise of natural science in the 17th century. The mechanical worldview and materialistic view of life created by so-called empirical philosophy and Enlightenment philosophy have already given rise to it. To put it further, when the dreams of capitalism were still without clues, the ideals of socialism, such as Confucius's Great Harmony and Plato's Republic, had already been established. The immature practice of socialism, as demonstrated by Morgan's theory of ancient society, had also been seen long ago. To go a step further, in the midst of the collapse of capitalism, the way out is not limited to one end of socialism. Social policies, fascism, and ideal technoocracy are all derived from this. It can be seen that socialism is just one kind of conversion of the direction of applying human knowledge and technology to cope with the control of capitalist forces, which is not enough to control society. Marx's materialistic view of history holds that when capitalism evolves to the point of natural collapse, the power of the proletariat will increase and communist socialism will be realized. However, the capitalist development of the former Tsarist Russia was not yet mature, and the Bolsheviks had already established the dictatorship of the proletariat. Was Marx wrong? Or is Lenin's dictatorship of the proletariat not Marx's doctrine, as Kautsky claimed? Although both of these prove my theory of the power of governance. Furthermore, some say that we do not despise Marx's entire theory because of this. After all, China's revolutionary theory needs a lot of interpretation from it.

In your reply, in addition to your attachment to socialism, you also showed your admiration for the Soviet Union. According to my speculation, you believe that China's way out lies in socialism, and the model of socialism is the Soviet Union. Indeed, the Soviet Union's achievements are different from those of Britain, the United States, and Germany. However, believing in it because of the general concept of its amazing achievements inevitably leads to superficiality. Since we know this, we should also know why. In other words, we should investigate the driving force behind its great achievements. To summarize, there are roughly the following points:

1. Organization of youth. According to the age distribution of the Soviet Union's population in 1900 (calculated per 1,000 people), in the European part, males aged 0 to 19 accounted for 249 per 1,000, and females accounted for 266 per 1,000. Males aged 20 to 59 accounted for 166 per 1,000, and females accounted for 241. Those over 59 accounted for 35 per 1,000 for males and 43 per 1,000 for females. In the Asian part, males aged 0-19 accounted for 256/1000, females accounted for 260/1000, males aged 20-59 for 191/1000, females for 219/1000, and the male and female population over 59 were each 37/1000. Based on these statistics, it can be inferred that the Soviet population is concentrated in young people and youths. Those who dominate society also understand this, and they are closely organizing and strictly training young people to be able to assume the great responsibilities of the revolution, such as the "October People," the Young Pioneers, the Communist Youth League, and the Communist Party, all of which have their important missions.

2. Special Dictatorship. The Soviet Union is commonly known as a country of national equality and the dictatorship of farmers and workers, but this is not the case. Lenin's Soviet Russia was not the communist society that Marx envisioned, and the Soviet Union in Stalin's era was even less so the Soviet Russia that Lenin built. The current Soviet Union is a dictatorship of the Communist Party on behalf of farmers and workers, and Stalin is a dictator on behalf of the Communist Party. These are all realities that do not need to be distinguished. For example, the Soviet Constitution stipulates that the Executive Committee is organized by the Nationalities Council and the Union Council. The Union Council representatives are elected in the Soviet Congress. The Nationalities Council is filled by representatives elected separately by various autonomous regions and autonomous republics. All resolutions of the Soviet Executive Committee must be unanimously agreed upon by the Nationalities Council, the Union Council, and the Executive Committee to be valid. Otherwise, a joint meeting will be held to mediate. This seems to be a creed to respect national self-determination and take into account the opinions of minority peoples. However, once mediation fails, the Executive Committee submits it to the Soviet Congress for final adjudication. The Soviet Congress allocates representatives based on population, and the Russian population accounts for almost three-quarters of the Soviet Union. The Soviet Congress should be the largest force in Russia and can control everything. Therefore, national self-determination is only Russian national self-determination. Although this kind of dictatorship has another value that makes people pay attention to it.

3. Planned Economy. The most obvious and dazzling achievement of the Soviet Union is the success of this planned economy. From Lenin's electrification plan to the five-year plan of progress, the world has already been amazed. This is the characteristic of the dominant power of the Soviet socialist country. It is true that today the dominant power of the Soviet Union has shifted the knowledge and technology of human evolution to another direction, that is, as you said, "planned, systematic, economical, and fully" development. As for the process and achievements, I believe that the people of the country know it well and do not need my elaboration.

4. Abolition of Private Ownership. The evils of capitalism, such as the plunder of surplus value and the accumulation of private capital, are all just the accomplices of this system of private property. Therefore, if we want to fundamentally eliminate the misfortunes of society, we must abolish the shackles of private ownership. The Soviet Union is the only country that has implemented this policy. For example, industries are nationalized, capital is state-owned, and foreign trade is also managed by the state. In addition, agricultural farms are established, such as establishing state-owned agricultural farms as a standard to encourage cooperative farms for practical results. As a result, both workers and farmers have a sense of national identity and automatically participate in production and control production. For example, the organization of various production shock brigades is a great help to the success of the five-year plan.

I have finished describing the characteristics of the Soviet Union. I think of China's way out today. In addition to a few special prerequisites, all the advantages are worthy of our adoption. However, I don't know if the people of the country have paid attention to it. As for how China's entire revolutionary theory should be, I originally wanted to briefly express one or two of my humble opinions here. However, I feel that the above article has already taken up a lot of space, and the number of words below is almost the same. I am afraid that it will hinder the public's right to communicate. I will wait for the next time to correct it. I don't know what your opinion is. I have often said that we are not afraid of mistakes. What we value is the ability to seek correctness from mistakes. We are not afraid of contradictions. What we value is the ability to seek harmony from contradictions. In this way, what in the world cannot be solved? The universe is changing, life is changing, and gentlemen strive for self-improvement. With respect, I wish you progress. (Reply will be published tomorrow)

Record of the First Day of the Astronomical, Mathematical, and Physical Discussion Meeting 166

Discussions divided into three groups in the morning and afternoon

(Nanjing, 1st) Sixty-odd people attended the opening session of the Ministry of Education's Astronomical, Mathematical, and Physical Discussion Meeting on the first. It was decided to divide the meeting into three groups: astronomy, mathematics, and physics. In the morning, the groups discussed various issues. Gao Lu presided over the discussion on the astronomy curriculum. It was decided that all universities should add astronomy courses, and high schools should also add an astronomy class. The mathematics group, chaired by Feng Zugou, was divided into four categories: translation of names, curriculum standards, compilation of single-volume books, a directory, and others. Feng Zugou, Jiang Lifu, Huang Jiyu, and Zheng Tongsun were appointed as the presidium. The physics group, chaired by Li Shuhua, decided not to divide into smaller groups. Fang Guangqi, Ding Xielin, Wei Xueren, Bao Youxun, and Zhou Changshou were appointed as proposal review committee members. The proposals were divided into seven categories: 1. Translation of names, 2. Curriculum standards, 3. Instrument manufacturing, 4. List of books that must be compiled and translated, 5. National defense, 6. Popular science education, 7. Others. The group meetings continued in the afternoon. The astronomy group, attended by eight people, was still chaired by Gao Lu. Four types of books that must be compiled were decided, and the issue of astronomical translations was discussed. The mathematics group, chaired by Zheng Tongsun and Huang Shouzhong, appointed Jiang Lifu, Gu Cheng, Hu Dunfu, Cao Qianyi, Sun Guangbi, and five others as members of the translation review committee. The minimum subjects for university mathematics courses were decided, and Feng Zugou, Sun Guangyuan, Bu Qing, Gu Cheng, and Yu Guanglang were appointed to draft the content of these minimum subjects. The physics group, chaired by Li Shuhua and recorded by Qian Baojun and Wang Zuoqing, decided on the principles and minimum subjects of the university physics curriculum and the content of these minimum subjects. In the evening, the Ministry of Education hosted a banquet at the Overseas Chinese Reception Center for all members of the meeting.

Jiangsu Education Fee Auditors Resolve to Rectify Education Fees 167

All counties that have not been divided should complete the division by the end of May. In late March, the Jiangsu Education Fee Auditors discussed how to handle the large amount of unpaid land tax, slaughter tax, and other taxes at the Education Fee Management Office. Regarding the land tax rectification method, the following resolutions were passed: (1) All counties that have not been divided should complete the division by the end of May (more than 20 counties have been divided). (2) Counties with outstanding payments should allocate temporary funds and construction equipment funds for primary and secondary schools as much as possible (the total amount of outstanding payments from various counties is 400,000 to 500,000 yuan, with Wuxi, Yixing, Songjiang, Liyang, and Wujin counties having the most, with each county owing 20,000 to 30,000 yuan). Regarding the slaughter tax method, the following resolutions were passed: Those who exceed one month of deposit will be urged to pay, and those who exceed two months will be urged to pay their guarantors. It was also resolved that supervisors who fail to report the report of the previous ten days will have their salaries deducted for the current month, and those who exceed three months will be replaced by the management office.

According to other news, the Jiangsu Education Fee Management Office has previously requested rewards for counties that have made efforts to pay education fees to the finance bureau, such as Changshu and Zhenjiang. It has now been found that Jiangyin, Kunshan, Shanghai (and several other counties) have cleared previous debts and do not owe new fees, which is commendable. The office has requested the Education Department to submit it to the provincial government for a conference reward.

Experts Conference 174

A special experts conference was held at the Ronghong Hall of the school yesterday at 9:00 AM. Attendees included former Minister of Transportation Ye Yuhu, Counselor of the Ministry of Railways Xia Guangyu, Director of the Ministry of Industry Liu Yinbo, experts from various fields, President of the school Li Zhaohuan, Dean of the School of Management Zhong Weicheng, Dean of the School of Electrical Engineering Zhang Tingjin, Dean of the School of Civil Engineering Li Qianruo, and professors Tan Bingxun, Wang Bingnan, Xiong Dahui, and Tang Xinji, totaling more than eighty people. It was truly an unprecedented grand gathering in China's academic circles. Mr. Corderoy, a British advisor to the Ministry of Railways, and Mr. Schfranek, the U.S. Commercial Counselor in China, also attended the meeting. President Li first introduced Ye Yuhu to the experts, and then Ye assumed the role of chairman of the conference and officially opened the meeting. The chairman delivered a lengthy opening speech, lasting nearly twenty minutes, which thoroughly discussed the scope of the prepared topics for the day, including industry, transportation, and national defense. Immediately afterward, the discussion of the papers began. There were four papers in total. The first paper was titled "Railways and National Defense." To facilitate discussion, Dean Zhong Weicheng, the author, stood up and briefly presented the main points of the paper. He offered many novel insights into the various errors of China's past railway national defense policies, especially his research on the railway network in the Northeast Provinces was the most precise. He also drafted future railway policies to strengthen national defense, stating that two central points should be established north and south of the Yangtze River, supplemented by a circular border defense railway starting from a certain point and ending at a certain point. At the end of the paper, two suggestions were attached regarding military transportation issues during the national crisis: one was a strategy for rebuilding military railways in the front lines, and the other was a method for centralizing railway military organizations. (The detailed content of the paper will not be publicly released due to the decision of the conference regarding national defense plans.) The second paper was titled "Industry, Transportation, and National Defense." The third paper was titled "The Relationship Between Establishing Steel Plants and National Defense." As the authors Wei Tingsheng and Huang Jintao were unable to attend due to other commitments, Tang Xinji and Shou Junliang respectively represented them in reading the papers. The fourth paper was "Industrial and Transportation Education and National Defense" by Ye Yuhu, which was also briefly explained by Tang Xinji. Afterward, Xiong Dahui, Tan Bingxun, and Wang Bingnan supplemented their opinions on national defense issues. Mr. Xiong spoke on "The Relationship Between Shipping and National Defense," Mr. Tan spoke on "The Relationship Between Telecommunications and National Defense," and Mr. Wang spoke on "The Relationship Between Aviation and National Defense." Finally, there was a free discussion. The experts spoke one after another, some speaking briefly but meaningfully, while others debated eloquently and vigorously. The discussion of various issues related to industry, transportation, and national defense was extremely detailed and thorough. It was a pity that the time limit of the meeting prevented further discussion. When discussing a certain issue related to national defense, several experts debated fiercely due to differing opinions, and it was difficult to reach a conclusion. Fortunately, the chairman made a final decision. Ye had a wealth of research on national defense issues and had already formed a clear plan, so even when encountering difficult problems, he was able to solve them easily. In addition, the four papers discussed yesterday totaled no less than one hundred thousand words, and the supplementary or revised opinions put forward by the experts were extremely complex. However, before the closing of the conference, Chairman Ye Yuhu was able to summarize the opinions of various parties in a hurried time of more than ten minutes, organizing thousands of threads into two major outlines and more than twenty minor items, so that the first meeting of the conference achieved an extremely satisfactory and valuable result.

Small Railway Bureau 175

The scale of this conference is magnificent, and the layout is particularly splendid. Among them, the most interesting thing is the small train winding around the school. All management of the small railway bureau, such as locomotive affairs, train services, and finance, are undertaken by students of the School of Management. The weather has been fine in recent days, and the number of visitors has increased sharply, making the trains even more crowded. Yesterday, Huang Boqiao, the director of the two railway bureaus, and Wang Shengsheng, the head of the locomotive department, visited the station to observe the equipment and management system of the small railway bureau and praised them deeply. They bought tickets to ride around the railway for a week and praised this small railway bureau as a miniature of the domestic railway.

First Shanghai Open Cross-Country Run 183

Route of six miles through Jiangwan fields

Participants include 12 teams from China, England, Russia, France, etc.

Chinese Baihong team is expected to win the team championship

The first Shanghai Open Cross-Country Championship, organized by the Shanghai Westerners' Sports Association, will be held near Hongkou Park at 11:00 AM this morning. The course is six miles. Twelve teams representing several countries, including China, England, France, and Russia, will participate, totaling more than eighty people. This is the first international cross-country run in Shanghai and is expected to be a grand event.

Full Route 184

The race will start at 11:00 AM sharp at the gate on Jiangwan Road, west of Hongkou Park, and proceed to Old Jiangwan Road, heading into the Jiangwan fields. It will cross the fields and small rivers, continue east, then turn north back to Old Jiangwan Road, then west to Xinjiangwan Road, and return to the starting point, for a total distance of approximately six miles.

Scoring Method 185

Each team is limited to six participants. The scores of the first four finishers will be counted, and the scores of the remaining two will not be counted. The scoring method is the same as the International Walking Race, using the ranking as the score. The team with the lowest score wins the championship. The championship is divided into individual and team categories.

Summary of Rules 186

Before the race, the organizers will mark the entire course with white paper. Athletes must follow the paper and cannot deviate more than twelve yards from the white paper. Cutting the course is not allowed. If two or more referees discover a violation, the athlete will be disqualified. Pacers are not allowed, and protests against the referees' decisions are not allowed.

Staff and Prizes 187

President Mike McKenna, Chief Referee Bai Lieqi, Referee Chief Lieutenant Li Te, Starter Slei, Timekeeper Li Silian, Secretary Xipeng. The championship team will receive a large silver shield donated by Harry White. The individual champion will receive a large silver cup donated by the British American Tobacco Company, which will be awarded by Mrs. Xipeng.

Championship Prediction 188

The Baihong, Russian, and British Agal teams are most likely to win the team championship, especially Baihong. Huang Sheng, Wang Zhenglin, and Niugebao are expected to compete for the individual championship. The winner will likely be one of these three.

Spring and Autumn

The Nine Terrains Chapter - Fire 194

— Xueming

I accidentally flipped through an old copy of Sun Tzu’s “Art of War” on the bookshelf. Coincidentally, it opened to the chapter on the “Nine Terrains.” I am not a military man, so why would I study military books? However, the two words “Nine Terrains,” which I found very unfamiliar, drew me in to read further. At first glance, it said…

"In the art of war, there are dispersive ground, facile ground, contentious ground, communicative ground, intersecting ground, serious ground, difficult ground, hemmed-in ground, and desperate ground. When a chieftain fights in his own territory, it is dispersive ground; When he penetrates into enemy territory, but not deeply, it is facile ground. That which can be gained or lost to advantage, is contentious ground; ground on which each side has liberty of movement, is communicative ground; ground which forms the key to three contiguous states, so that he who occupies it first has most of the empire at his command, is intersecting ground; when one penetrates deeply into hostile territory, leaving a number of fortified cities in his rear, it is serious ground; mountain forests, precipitous passes, marshes and swamps—all ground that is hard to traverse: this is difficult ground; ground which is reached through narrow gorges, and from which we can only retire by tortuous paths, so that a small number of the enemy would suffice to crush a large body of our men: this is hemmed-in ground; ground on which we can only be saved from destruction by fighting without delay, is desperate ground……”

Based on this, let's compare it with the current Sino-Japanese war.

In the past, the feudal lords each occupied a territory, raised troops to protect themselves, which is exactly the same as the current warlords. Internal wars such as the Fengzhi War, in which soldiers left the customs, took the three northeastern provinces as dispersive ground, making the villages desolate and the people’s lives difficult. After the Feng army won, they became arrogant and lazy, so the September 18th Incident occurred. The iron hooves of the Japanese Empire crushed Shenyang, and the Chinese army lost the facile ground due to non-resistance. If a counterattack had been launched at that time, it would not have been difficult to recover the lost territory; but no, even the rich areas of Jilin and Heilongjiang were completely abandoned, and the army retreated to Jinzhou, which was still in a superior position in terms of offense and defense. Who knew that later even Jinzhou and Shanhaiguan, a famous city and fortress, a territory which could be fought over militarily, or traded in, would fall one after another? At this time, traitors and rebels took the opportunity to organize a puppet state, raping public opinion and occupying a land with tens of millions of people. Now that the intersecting ground has been lost, the general of non-resistance only realized that non-resistance was a bad strategy, and then concentrated the opium army in the mountainous and hidden province of Rehe. You also know that if you want to recover the lost land of the three eastern provinces, you must defend Rehe to the death. According to Sun Tzu, this is already "serious ground" and "difficult ground." Unfortunately, Mr. Tang Yulin ended up giving it away. Now our anti-Japanese army is fighting along the Great Wall. Xifengkou protrudes from the front, and the left and right wings have approached the Great Wall, while the enemy takes Chengde as its base camp, using winding and narrow mountain paths, which can be used for offense and defense. Our vanguard seems to be in danger of being defeated or encircled; if there is such an unfavorable situation and we are caught in a hemmed-in ground, we can only retreat and abandon the Great Wall. At that time, when we close our eyes and think about it, what will the situation be? Therefore, if we do not actively counterattack now, we will inevitably fall into a "desperate ground." The gate is wide open, the art of war is exhausted, and North China is in danger! North of the Yellow River, I am afraid that heroes will have no place to use their strength. Isn’t it too far from what Sun Tzu said, "A good fighter puts himself in an invincible position"? Some people say: When the Han general Han Xin fought against the Zhao state, in the Battle of Jingxingkou, he fought with his back to the river, called it "putting himself in a desperate ground and then surviving, putting himself in a lost ground and then surviving." Then, does that mean that the Chinese anti-Japanese war has no "nine terrains," and is that the way it will be? Can China be revived like this?

What kind of person is Pu Yi 196

— Pingcao

Pu Yi, who served as the puppet of Japan and assumed the role of executive of the puppet state, has long been famous. However, what kind of person he actually is, I am afraid that ordinary people cannot guess. I neither have Zheng Xiaoxu's qualifications to be a traitor, nor do I have Hu Shih's doctoral title to have the honor of visiting the palace. Of course, I don't know very well either. However, I have read his manuscript and can make a little judgment. Last year, I was in Beiping, and two cents could get a ticket to visit the Palace Museum. Coincidentally, what was open that day was the Qianqing Palace. The Hall of Longevity and Happiness inside the Qianqing Palace was Pu Yi's former bedroom. Although the person is gone and the building is empty, his handwriting still exists. Historical essays, letters, diaries, and other small pieces are all complete. Although they are not as sad and lingering as Li Houzhu of the Tang Dynasty, they are as funny and ridiculous as Liu Houzhu of Shu. Therefore, at that time, I took the trouble to copy a few excerpts.

It seems that Pu Yi is like a person who is determined to revive the country. His "On the Restoration of Guangwu" begins with these sentences: "Who in the world does not want to restore the country? But is restoration not difficult? However, Guangwu is very wrong..." He is also concerned about Eastern and Western cultures, so he also understands English. In his letters to his wife, the salutations are a combination of Chinese and Western styles: "My dear Waifu... You's Husband Pu Yi." Not only does he understand English, but he also knows rhyme. Please see his "Peach Blossom Palace Poem": "Peach Blossom Palace, Peach Blossom Courtyard, a peach blossom fairy lives in the Peach Blossom Courtyard, a peach blossom face, a peach blossom face, peach blossom scabies grow on the peach blossom face." What is even more important is that the talents he recruited included both new and old. Not only did Zheng Xiaoxu revise his papers for him, but Hu Shih, the dean of the Faculty of Arts of Peking University, was also often met. Therefore, Dr. Hu's business card is still in a glass frame, with a line of neat small characters written on it: "I have something to do today and cannot visit the palace." From this, we can know what kind of person Pu Yi is and to what extent his knowledge is. We can only pity his ignorance for his actions. Later, he even became a puppet, which is a manifestation of his ignorance.

Cold Mouth Ballad 197

— Clear and Gaunt

Cold Mouth is the center of today's battlefield, but its location has no verifiable record in ancient times. According to the Unified Gazetteer, during the Tang Dynasty, the Khitan soldiers were defeated and used the Cold Hinge to defend themselves. During the Song Dynasty, the Jin people exiled Hong Hao to Cold Mountain. Could this be Cold Mouth? I heard that there was a woman on the front lines who presented a white blade to the enemy. Slender jade hands, shimmering sword light, red blood and white snow flying in the air, presenting a unique, splendid, tragic scene. Looking out at the rivers and mountains, my heart is on the verge of breaking, so I compose this poem:

I have heard of resisting enemies with guns, not knives, and if resisting with knives, the enemy cries out in alarm. A woman roars with arms bared, like an angry tiger. The sound of killing rises everywhere, and all are heroes. The enemy faces it, the enemy's soul breaks, cowering in heaven and earth with nowhere to flee, falling to the ground and bowing a hundred times, the sound almost swallowed. Jade hands chop the neck, but the knife leaves no mark. In an instant, the sword light rises like fire, and the icy world begins to clear. The military spirit soars, washing away the enemy's aura, slicing open the enemy's liver, dismembering the enemy's body, separating the enemy's intestines, sucking the enemy's marrow. Why was the enemy so brave yesterday and so weak today? Now I know that the Wokou's military strength is great, but please try my sword. Otherwise, what will be the end of the enemy's forces!

Before Cold Mouth, who goes to battle? The sound of cannons is like a warning. Outside Cold Mouth, the enemy throws bombs endlessly. Cold Mouth freezes into ice flowers, and the sand and grass are covered in morning glow. The wind at Cold Mouth is like a tiger, the sword light whirling like snow, swallowing grease in a dance. One slash takes off the head, another slash hits the ground like a severed foot. At that moment, I hate not eating their flesh, drawing the knife across and stabbing their belly, kneeling before me is only shameful. Writhing in death, there is no crying allowed, collect the canine teeth and clothe them in blood, how tragic, the four limbs all cramped and shrunken. I hope the battlefield will be quickly recovered, so the enemy may finally close their eyes in peace. Red snow flowers cover the fields around Cold Mouth, in later years they will all tell of the great sword's merits.

Bloody Peach Blossoms 199

— Rong Yu

Jiangnan is truly a beautiful landscape. Look at the peach blossoms in March, which adorn the beautiful rivers and mountains, enticing people to become intoxicated and infatuated by them. Poets ponder them, painters sketch them, travelers carry their cameras to photograph them, and literati spread paper and dip ink to write their biographies. The frivolous peach blossoms possess such magic power.

In the end, are people pursuing peach blossoms, or are peach blossoms luring people? If I were a judge and both parties brought their case before me, I would definitely and unhesitatingly judge: "The opening of peach blossoms is for the struggle for life. Human appreciation is actually a sign of covetous ambition. In the future, all appreciation of peach blossoms will be prohibited." Such a judgment is neither arbitrary nor biased. Because to protect the weak nation and restrain the strong's ambition, it must be done this way.

In these years, flamboyant peach blossoms cannot heal the pain of lost land or save the tragedy of national subjugation. What do we appreciate about them? If we have the leisure and interest to appreciate peach blossoms, why not go to Guanwai (outside the Great Wall) to appreciate the blood flowers of soldiers, which can also arouse common hatred and inspire the heart to kill the enemy. From Jiu Men in the east to Gubei in the west, outside the Great Wall is full of iron cavalry. They have new-style killing weapons, and we only have flesh bombs of loyalty and patriotism. These many flesh bombs, carrying broadswords and bare-chested, advance, advance, advance in the smoke and flames; kill, kill, kill in the rain of bullets. The enemy truly collapses at the mere sight, and our flesh bombs also die for righteousness. The result is that many peach blossoms made of blood are sprinkled on the desolate yellow sand and the white snowy mountains. Are the peach blossoms in Jiangnan good? Are the peach blossoms on the edge of the Great Wall good? Please go and appreciate them. I remember there were two lines of poetry in the past: "Peach blossoms behind the horse and snow in front of the horse, how can one not look back?" This kind of poetry is too decadent! It makes people too short of breath! Now I will change it a bit: "Peach blossoms behind the horse and blood in front of the horse, how can peach blossoms compare to blood flowers' redness?" Compatriots, don't be greedy for the peach blossoms of Jiangnan, quickly go and appreciate the blood flowers outside Guanwai.

The Most Artistic Country 200

— He Jiagan

Our China's greatest, most enduring, and most widespread "art" is men dressing as women. The preciousness of this art lies in its being two-faced, or what is called "the Doctrine of the Mean." Men see "dressing as women," and women see "men dressing." On the surface, it is neutral, but in its bones, it is of course still male. However, if it doesn't dress up, will it become art? For example, China's inherent culture is the imperial examination system, plus the purchase of official titles. At first, it was said that this was too unlike democracy and did not conform to the trends of the times, so it dressed up as the Republic of China. However, this Republic has been in disrepair for a long time, and even the signboard has been peeled off, like the rouge on a female performer's face. This is disloyal to the nation and unfilial to the ancestors, and it is extremely reactionary. Now that we have long returned to the "trend of the times" of restoring our inherent culture, how can we allow such disloyalty and unfilial piety? Therefore, we must dress up once again. The draft is as follows: First, whoever has the qualifications to represent the people must be decided by examination. Second, after the successful candidates are selected, they will be selected again. This is called selecting (verb) the successful candidates; and the successful candidates who are selected will naturally be the elected people. According to grammar, the electors of such a National Assembly should be called "those who elect," and the elected people should be called "the selected successful candidates." But, if it doesn't dress up, will it become art? Therefore, they must dress up as the electors and those who are elected in a constitutional country, even though in essence they are still scholars and successful candidates. The deep meaning of this draft lies here: to let the masses see democracy, and to let the nation's ancestors see loyalty and filial piety; loyalty to the inherent imperial examination system, and filial piety to the ancestors who established the imperial examination system. In addition, the democracy that has already been realized in Shanghai is that only those who pay taxes have the right to elect and be elected, so that only 4,465 large citizens are left in vast Shanghai. This is like the purchase of official titles — those with money are the masters, but they will definitely pass the imperial examination, and even if they don't take a supplementary exam, they will be granted the title of "Successful Candidate," because the example under the foreign masters should be followed, not to mention that this is also one side that does not violate the inherent culture, while at the same time dressing up very much like constitutional democracy. This is one.

Secondly, negotiating while resisting: looking at it from this side, it is resistance, but looking at it from that side, it is actually negotiation. Thirdly, on the one hand, being industrialists and bankers, and on the other hand, claiming to be "just a little poor." Fourthly, on the one hand, the sales of Japanese goods are booming again, and on the other hand, telling people that it is "National Goods Year"… There are countless such examples, and most of them are performed very skillfully, with both sides being smooth.

Ah, China is truly the most artistic country and the most moderate nation.

However, the common people are still dissatisfied. Alas, the moderation of the gentleman is the opposite of the moderation of the petty man!

White Russian 201

— Zhou Lengjia

I left the house, walked through a narrow, dark alley, and arrived at Avenue Joffre. A person came towards me and took off his hat. It was a White Russian.

I knew him. He was doing a job similar to begging on this road. Every day I walked on this road, I had to see him, and he always had to take off his hat to me.

I didn't know his surname or given name, just as he didn't know me. I couldn't ask him in Russian, and he couldn't beg me in Chinese. On the surface, he and I were completely estranged.

But in our hearts, we had many things in common. Every time he saw me and took off his hat, he always smiled at me. This smile contained bitterness. From this smile, I could see his past extravagance and his current plight.

However, I never gave him anything, because I didn't know if giving to a Russian beggar was the same as giving to a Chinese beggar. So sometimes, even though I had pockets full of money, I always hesitated to take it out. I don't know when, I suddenly had the idea of pitying him. At that time, he was smiling at me, holding the hat he had taken off in one hand, and extending his thumb and little finger, placing them beside his mouth. I suddenly woke up and couldn't help asking him:

"Do you want to smoke?"

He didn't seem to understand me, and nodded subconsciously, still smiling. I started leading him to the front of a cigarette paper store, spent ten cents, and bought him a pack of "Wuhua Brand" cigarettes. He took it, his lips moved, his eyes staring at me blankly, his eyes full of gratitude.

After that, it became a routine. Every day when he saw me, he would always put his thumb and little finger beside his mouth; and I would always have to spend ten cents to buy him a pack of "Wuhua Brand" cigarettes.

But my financial resources were limited after all. As the days went by, I couldn't even afford to supply him with a pack of "Wuhua Brand" cigarettes every day. Today, I met him again on Avenue Joffre, this foreign friend (I prefer to call him a friend, and I don't want to have a gentleman-like friend). He was still smiling, taking off his hat, and putting his thumb and little finger beside his mouth; but I finally steeled myself and patted my pocket to show him that I no longer had the power to continue supplying him. His face suddenly became dejected, and he shook the hand that was originally placed beside his mouth, and walked away silently and sadly.

Looking at his back, all the humble lives and pitiful situations of the weak rushed to my heart, making my soul hurt as if it were injured. I felt that even that shaking hand of his carried his kind soul and kind heart. I repented, but he had already gone far away.

Suddenly a question rushed into my brain: "Living in my current national environment, how much difference is there between me and him in the eyes of the strong?"

A newspaper boy came walking towards me, shouting loudly the news of the loss of Jehol.

Women of Tibet 202

— Qi Zhi

In today's world where monogamy is prevalent, polyandry is still practiced in Tibet. The reason why this unreasonable marriage system has survived to this day, of course, has its own reasons. Summarizing the general opinion, there are roughly two reasons for the prevalence of polyandry in Tibet. Some people say that there are fewer women than men in the Tibetan population, and because there are not enough to distribute, they have to adopt this system. In fact, Tibet has neither household registration surveys nor population statistics, so how can one say whether there are more or fewer men or women? This is probably just a speculation by some travelers or sociologists from various European and American countries. Others say that the reason for the prevalence of polyandry in Tibet lies in economic relations. Because resources are scarce and production is difficult in the region, it is not easy to accumulate wealth. Wealthy families, in order to preserve their ancestral property, have to strive for unity, so there are often five or six brothers who marry one wife together. Conversely, poor families can marry one wife per person. This statement seems to be more in line with the facts than the former.

The women of Tibet can be divided into two parts: urban women and rural women. The main tasks of rural women are farming, herding, collecting firewood, and transporting goods. They do not apply powder or makeup, and they bury themselves in hard work all day long, appearing strong and ugly, with brown-black skin, but they are extremely simple. Urban women are very different. Let's take the situation in Lhasa, the capital of Tibet, as an example. The women of Lhasa can be divided into four classes: First, aristocratic women. They have beautiful looks and graceful manners, are skilled in singing and dancing, and are also very lively. Their jewelry is all made of gold, jade, coral, and pearls, and their makeup is the most extravagant. Second, middle-class women. They run small businesses, open small shops, and sell silk, cloth, and sundries. When they do business, they are good at telling false prices, and they also use warm emotions to intoxicate customers, so it is easy to sell their goods at good prices. Third, lower-class women. Tibet has private prostitutes who engage in flesh trade, but there are no public brothels. Some young women from ordinary families, because their wedding date is approaching and they have not yet secured the funds for their dowry, do not hesitate to sell their bodies to exchange money to prepare their dowry. This is truly a strange custom. Fourth, nuns. In general families in Lhasa, if there are two or more daughters, they must choose one to shave her head and become a nun, sending her to a nunnery to practice hard for the rest of her life, and women who become nuns seem to be quite willing.

In "Midnight," most of these Chinese "people" are still under the deception, deception, and oppression of "dogs," but they are already fighting and resisting. Their weakness is not that they don't want to resist themselves, but that they are mostly not good at jumping out of all kinds of conspiracies of "dogs," and all kinds of indirect or indirect dog-inspired influences. For example, they clearly think it is already broad daylight even though it is still midnight, and even think that the sun is about to set, so they desperately hurry on, fearing that once night comes again, they will never see the light of day. Of course, not every "person" thinks this way. These are just some "people" rushing in front of the masses. The masses are learning in practice.

Gold Standard in the Financial Storm 206

Overseas Silver Prices and Exchange Rates Both Fall, Producing a High Price of 1100 Yuan - Central Bullish Sentiment Emerges Before Closing, but Sees a Fall of 11.9 Yuan

Although the gold market was only open for half a day yesterday, its changes were extremely rapid, with prices first rising and then falling in a very volatile process. Initially, foreign dispatches indicated that London's major silver contracts for both near and far terms were down 1.875, New York silver prices were down a small 0.25, far term silver market fell over 0.3 percent, Anglo-American exchange rates fell 1.125 points, American-British also fell a small 1.3125 points, bank private dispatches fell 3.125 points, and American cotton also fell a small 0.6 pound. Therefore, raw transactions immediately jumped, once reaching 1100 yuan and slightly declining, with the opening price at 1096 yuan. The exchange market opened tight, so the initial fluctuations were not significant, but the trend seemed stable. Later, due to Mitsui eating in July U.S. dollars at 0.95 yuan, market sentiment was extremely good, and prices immediately rose to 1100 yuan, which was a new high. However, the exchange market did not have better transactions, and those making sell-offs gradually retreated. The HSBC official exchange rate revealed first a small 0.25 for the pound, and a small 0.375 for the U.S. dollar, slightly pulling up. However, banks tended to become congested, and Sino-French came out with July U.S. dollars at 0.95625 yuan, still in a downstream shape. However, at this time, banks occasionally conducted offsetting transactions, so the process was still even. When Banque Franco-Chinoise (Hua Bi) sold July U.S. dollars at 0.96875 yuan and broke the 90 yuan barrier, it was unexpected that once this barrier was broken, the sharp decline became even more severe. Da De Cheng, Da Xing Yong, Qian Chang Xiang, and others aggressively sold off, coming on strong. Gold prices could not withstand it and retreated step by step. Rumors spread in the market about the Central Bank releasing bullish positions and various deteriorating situations, causing panic and a rapid decline in prices. The exchange market also became very firm, and because banks were willing to sell July U.S. dollars at 0.98125 yuan, breaking the 80 yuan barrier, Fu Chang sold even more, leading to a fall to 1075 yuan, a decrease of 25 yuan from the highest price. The declining trend gradually stopped, and those buying in at low prices seemed to surge, so the closing price at noon was 1077.5 yuan. Upon investigation, the market situation during the half-day rose and fell again, mainly because the Central Bank aggressively sold U.S. dollars. Spot red also changed lower to an additional 0.75 yuan and 0.5 yuan, and the swap premium was reduced to 15.5 yuan and 12.5 yuan. The market situation during the half-day is recorded below:

The morning opening was 1096 yuan, an increase of 6.6 yuan compared to the previous close. Commodity opened at 6.5 yuan. The exchange market opened with the pound at 1 shilling, 8 pence, 0.1875, tighter by 0.125 compared to the previous close, and the U.S. dollar at 0.88125 yuan, tighter by 0.1875 compared to the previous close. Fu Chang first sold bars, retreating from 6.8 yuan to 5.2 yuan. Heng Xing placed a limit order to buy, and was held back. Shunli Run Chang Yu further went up to around 7 yuan, Zhi Feng Yong advanced to 7.5 yuan, Yuan Mao Yong came to sell and retreated to 6 yuan. After this, a sharp upward trend was seen. (Tianjin) Military telephone, still connected to Haiyang Town at noon on the 2nd. Our Shimenzhai position changed on the night of the 1st. (Special dispatch on the 2nd)

(Beiping) The fighting at Shimenzhai is extremely fierce. Enemy aircraft dropped countless bombs on the 1st. Our troops engaged in hand-to-hand combat with the enemy four or five times, with countless casualties, a truly tragic situation. On the morning of the 2nd, 14 enemy aircraft again flew over Shimenzhai, bombing and strafing, unprecedented in previous battles.
